Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(1)(c)(vi): emergency expenditures;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(1)(c)(vii): expenditures from all other fund or subfund sources;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(1)(c)(viii): transfers or appropriations from the Income Tax Fund to the Uniform School Fund;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(1)(c)(ix): 63J-1-312 transfers into, or appropriations made to, the General Fund Budget Reserve Account established in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(1)(c)(x): 63J-1-313 transfers into, or appropriations made to, the Income Tax Fund Budget Reserve Account established in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(1)(c)(xi): 63J-1-314; 65A-8-204; 65A-8-215; 53-2a-603 transfers in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(1)(c)(xii): 63A-5b-401 money appropriated to fund the total one-time project costs for the construction of capital development projects as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(1)(c)(xiii): 72-2-118 transfers or deposits into or appropriations made to the Centennial Highway Fund created by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(1)(c)(xiv): 72-2-124 transfers or deposits into or appropriations made to the Transportation Investment Fund of 2005 created by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(1)(c)(xv): transfers or deposits into or appropriations made to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(1)(c)(xv)(A): the Department of Transportation from any source; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(1)(c)(xv)(B): any transportation-related account or fund from any source; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(1)(c)(xvi): supplemental appropriations from the General Fund to the Division of Forestry, Fire, and State Lands to provide money for wildland fire control expenses incurred during the current or previous fire years.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(2): "Base year real per capita appropriations" means the result obtained for the state by dividing the fiscal year 1985 actual appropriations of the state less debt money by:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(2)(a): the state's July 1, 1983 population; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(2)(b): the fiscal year 1983 inflation index divided by 100.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(3): "Calendar year" means the time period beginning on January 1 of any given year and ending on December 31 of the same year.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(4): "Fiscal emergency" means an extraordinary occurrence requiring immediate expenditures and includes the settlement under Laws of Utah 1988, Fourth Special Session, Chapter 4.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(5): "Fiscal year" means the time period beginning on July 1 of any given year and ending on June 30 of the subsequent year.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(6): "Fiscal year 1985 actual base year appropriations" means fiscal year 1985 actual capital and operations appropriations from General Fund and non-Uniform School Fund income tax revenue sources, less debt money.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(7): 63J-3-202 "Inflation index" means the change in the general price level of goods and services as measured by the Gross National Product Implicit Price Deflator of the Bureau of Economic Analysis, U.S. Department of Commerce calculated as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(8): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(8)(a): "Maximum allowable appropriations limit" means the appropriations that could be, or could have been, spent in any given year under the limitations of this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(8)(b): "Maximum allowable appropriations limit" does not mean actual appropriations spent or actual expenditures.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(9): "Most recent fiscal year's inflation index" means the fiscal year inflation index two fiscal years previous to the fiscal year for which the maximum allowable inflation and population appropriations limit is being computed under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(10): "Most recent fiscal year's population" means the fiscal year population two fiscal years previous to the fiscal year for which the maximum allowable inflation and population appropriations limit is being computed under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(11): 63J-3-202 "Population" means the number of residents of the state as of July 1 of each year as calculated by the Governor's Office of Planning and Budget according to the procedures and requirements of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(12): "Revenues" means the revenues of the state from every tax, penalty, receipt, and other monetary exaction and interest connected with it that are recorded as unrestricted revenue of the General Fund and from non-Uniform School Fund income tax revenues, except as specifically exempted by this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-103(13): "Security" means any bond, note, warrant, or other evidence of indebtedness, whether or not the bond, note, warrant, or other evidence of indebtedness is or constitutes an "indebtedness" within the meaning of any provision of the constitution or laws of this state.


Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-201 Appropriations limit -- Formula.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-201(1): There is established a state appropriations limit for each fiscal year beginning after June 30, 1988.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-201(2): For each of these fiscal years, the annual legislative appropriations for this state, its agencies, departments, and institutions may not exceed that sum determined by applying the formula B* P* (I/100) in which:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-201(2)(a): "B" equals the base year real per capita appropriations for the state, its agencies, departments, and institutions;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-201(2)(b): "P" equals the most recent fiscal year's population; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-201(2)(c): "I" equals the most recent fiscal year's inflation index adjusted to reflect fiscal year 1989 as having an index value of 100.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-201(3): 63J-3-205 The revenues specified in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-202 Computing formula elements.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-202(1): For purposes of calculating fiscal year inflation indexes for the previous fiscal year, the Governor's Office of Planning and Budget shall use:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-202(1)(a): the actual quarterly data released by the U.S. Department of Commerce as of January 31 of each year; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-202(1)(b): the most recent U.S. Bureau of Census population estimates as of January 31 of each year.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-202(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-202(2)(a): For purposes of computing the inflation index, the Governor's Office of Planning and Budget shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-202(2)(a)(i): assign the bureau's 1982 calendar year inflation index value of 100 to fiscal year 1989 for purposes of computing fiscal year index values;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-202(2)(a)(ii): compute all subsequent fiscal year inflation indexes after having assigned the fiscal year 1989 inflation index a value of 100; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-202(2)(a)(iii): use the quarterly index values published by the Bureau of Economic Analysis, U.S. Department of Commerce, to compute fiscal year index values.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-202(2)(b): If the bureau changes its calendar base year, appropriate adjustments are to be made in this chapter to accommodate those changes.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-202(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-202(3)(a): For purposes of computing the most recent fiscal year's population, the Governor's Office of Planning and Budget shall convert the April 1 decennial census estimate to a July 1 estimate, unless otherwise estimated by the Bureau of Census.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-202(3)(b): If the bureau changes the state's July 1, 1983 base year population after it conducts the 1990 Census, appropriate adjustments shall be made in this chapter to accommodate those changes.


Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-203 Program and service adjustments to the limitation -- Funding level.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-203(1): If the state transfers partial or total responsibility of a program or service to another unit of government, the appropriations limitations shall be decreased by the amount of the transfer.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-203(2): If the state accepts partial or total responsibility for a program or service from another unit of government, the appropriations limit shall be increased by the amount of the transfer.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-203(3): If funding exempted under this chapter for a program or service administered by the state is reduced or eliminated and the Legislature elects to fund the program or service with tax revenue, the appropriations limitations shall be increased by the amount the Legislature elects to fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-203(4): If the state transfers the funding source of a program or service from taxes to user charges or other exempted revenue sources specified in this chapter, the maximum allowable appropriations limitations shall be decreased by the amount of the transfer.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-203(5): If the Legislature transfers the funding source of a program or service from user charges or other exempted revenue sources as specified in this chapter to tax revenues, appropriations limitations shall be increased by the amount of the transfer.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-203(6): If the state transfers revenues from sources exempt under this chapter to funds containing revenues from nonexempt sources, the revenues transferred shall be part of and subject to the appropriations limits of this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-204 Exceptions to limitation -- Fiscal emergency -- Requirements -- Limits modified or exceeded by vote of the people.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-204(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-204(1)(a): The limits as provided in this chapter may be exceeded if a fiscal emergency is declared.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-204(1)(b): A fiscal emergency for the state shall be declared by the governor and confirmed by more than two-thirds of both houses of the Legislature.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-204(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-204(2)(a): Funding for fiscal emergencies may not be included in the appropriations base for computing the maximum allowable appropriations in subsequent years.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-204(2)(b): Fiscal emergency appropriations shall remain separate from appropriations subject to limits imposed by this chapter and shall be assigned expiration dates.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-204(3): Any limit in this chapter may be exceeded or modified by a majority vote of the people in a statewide election.


Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-205 Money excluded from the limitation.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Money from the following sources is excluded from the revenues appropriated and used in determining a limitation:Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-205(1): money received from the government of the United States including federal mineral lease payments;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-205(2): money received by the state from another unit of government, except the proceeds of taxes, fees, or penalties imposed by the state and collected by the other unit of government;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-205(3): money derived from the issuance of, or to pay interest, principal, or redemption premiums on, any security;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-205(4): money received from the sale of fixed assets or gains on fixed asset transfers;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-205(5): the proceeds of contracts, grants, gifts, donations, and bequests made to the state for a purpose specified by the contractor or donor;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-205(6): user charges derived by the state from the sale of a product or service pledged or legally available to repay any security or for which the quantity of the product or level of service provided to a user is at the discretion of the user; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-205(7): money raised to meet fiscal emergencies.

Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-301 State auditor's responsibilities with respect to the limitation -- Correction of deficiencies.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The state auditor shall notify the state through the appropriate officer or officers of necessary corrective action if upon audit or examination of the results of an independent audit or a budget document of the state, the state auditor determines that:Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-301(1): funds have been improperly accounted or budgeted for in order to avoid the limitations imposed by this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-301(2): funds have been improperly exempted from the limitations as provided in this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-301(3): general government functions have been improperly financed by user or service charges; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-3-301(4): the limitations imposed by this chapter have been exceeded.

Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401 Planning coordinator appointment, functions, and duties.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(1)(a): The executive director shall appoint a planning coordinator to perform the functions and duties stated in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(1)(b): The planning coordinator serves at the pleasure of and under the direction of the executive director.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(2): The planning coordinator shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(2)(a): act as the governor's adviser on state, regional, metropolitan, and local governmental planning matters relating to public improvements and land use;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(2)(b): counsel with the authorized representatives of the Department of Transportation, the Division of Facilities Construction and Management, the Department of Health, the Department of Workforce Services, the Labor Commission, the Department of Natural Resources, the School and Institutional Trust Lands Administration, and other proper persons concerning all state planning matters;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(2)(c): when designated to do so by the governor, receive funds made available to the state by the federal government;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(2)(d): receive, review, and provide an internet-accessible repository of plans and studies of the various state agencies and political subdivisions relating to public improvements, housing, land use, economic development, transportation infrastructure, water infrastructure, and utility infrastructure;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(2)(e): if a conflict occurs between the plans and proposals of state agencies, prepare specific recommendations for the resolution of the conflict and submit the recommendations to the governor for a decision resolving the conflict;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(2)(f): if a conflict occurs between the plans and proposals of a state agency and a political subdivision or between two or more political subdivisions, advise these entities of the conflict and make specific recommendations for the resolution of the conflict;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(2)(g): act as the governor's planning agent in planning public improvements and land use and, in this capacity, undertake special studies and investigations, participate in cross-jurisdictional planning activities, and, if needed, provide coordination;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(2)(h): provide information and cooperate with the Legislature or any of its committees in conducting planning studies;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(2)(i): cooperate and exchange information with federal agencies and local, metropolitan, or regional agencies as necessary to assist with federal, state, regional, metropolitan, and local programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(2)(j): make recommendations to the governor that the planning coordinator considers advisable for the proper development and coordination of plans for state government and political subdivisions;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(2)(k): assist in the interpretation of projections and analyses with respect to future growth needs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(2)(l): actively participate in informing the short-term and long-term budgetary needs of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(3): (3)(b); (3)(a)(iii)
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(3)(a): (3)(b) The planning coordinator may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(3)(a)(i): perform regional and state planning and assist state government planning agencies in performing state planning;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(3)(a)(ii): provide planning assistance to Indian tribes regarding planning for Indian reservations;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(3)(a)(iii): (3)(b) assist city, county, metropolitan, and regional planning agencies in performing local, metropolitan, and regional planning, subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(3)(a)(iv): conduct, or coordinate with stakeholders to conduct, public meetings or hearings to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(3)(a)(iv)(A): encourage maximum public understanding of and agreement with the factual data and assumptions upon which projections and analyses are based; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(3)(a)(iv)(B): receive suggestions as to the types of projections and analyses that are needed.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(3)(b): (3)(a)(iii) In performing the duties described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-401(4): 63L-11-201 In assisting in the preparation of plans, policies, programs, or processes related to the management or use of federal lands or natural resources on federal lands in the state, the planning coordinator shall coordinate with the Public Lands Policy Coordinating Office created in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-802 Creation of COVID-19 Local Assistance Matching Grant Program -- Eligibility -- Duties of the office.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-802(1): There is established a grant program known as COVID-19 Local Assistance Matching Grant Program that is administered by the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-802(2): (3) The office shall award financial grants to local governments that meet the qualifications described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-802(2)(a): projects or services that address the economic impacts of the COVID-19 emergency on housing insecurity, lack of affordable housing, or homelessness;

Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-802(2)(d): any other purpose authorized under the American Rescue Plan Act.

Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-802(3)(b): (2) certify that the local government will spend grant funds:

Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-802(4): As soon as is practicable, but on or before September 15, 2021, the office shall, with recommendations from the review committee, establish:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-802(4)(a): procedures for applying for and awarding grants under this part, using an online grants management system that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-802(4)(a)(i): manages each grant throughout the duration of the grant;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-802(4)(a)(ii): allows for:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-802(4)(a)(ii)(A): online submission of grant applications; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-802(4)(a)(ii)(B): auditing and reporting for a local government that receives grant funds; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-802(4)(a)(iii): generates reports containing information about each grant;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-802(4)(b): criteria for awarding grants; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-802(4)(c): reporting requirements for grant recipients.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-802(5): Subject to appropriation, the office shall award grant funds on a competitive basis until December 31, 2024.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-802(6): (4); 63J-4-803 Before November 30 of each year, ending November 30, 2025, the office shall submit a report to the Executive Appropriations Committee that includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-802(6)(a): (4) a summary of the procedures, criteria, and requirements established under Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-802(6)(e): the aggregate amount of grant funds awarded under the grant program during the previous year; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-802(6)(f): any other information the office considers relevant to evaluating the success of the grant program.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-4-802(7): The office may use funds appropriated by the Legislature for the grant program to pay for administrative costs.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 63J - Chapter 5 - Federal Funds Procedures Act
**************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1): As used in this chapter:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(a)(i): "Agency" means a department, division, committee, commission, council, court, or other administrative subunit of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(a)(ii): "Agency" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(a)(ii)(A): executive branch entities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(a)(ii)(B): judicial branch entities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(a)(ii)(C): the State Board of Education.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(a)(iii): "Agency" does not mean higher education institutions or political subdivisions.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(b): "Contingency disclosure and plan" means, with respect to a federal funds reauthorization or new federal funds request, the submitting or requesting agency's:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(b)(i): disclosure of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(b)(i)(A): the likelihood that the amount or value of the federal funds will be reduced, and how that likelihood changes over time; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(b)(i)(B): the likelihood that the federal funds will become unavailable, and how that likelihood changes over time;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(b)(ii): explanation of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(b)(ii)(A): whether accepting the federal funds may create an expectation of ongoing funding by any beneficiary of the funds; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(b)(ii)(B): as applicable, how the agency will communicate to stakeholders that services funded by the federal funds may or will be temporary;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(b)(iii): plan for how the agency will:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(b)(iii)(A): proceed if the amount or value of the federal funds are unexpectedly reduced in any material degree or amount;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(b)(iii)(B): proceed if the federal funds become unavailable unexpectedly;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(b)(iii)(C): wind down the program or services funded by the federal funds when the federal funds are exhausted; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(b)(iii)(D): transition any beneficiaries of the funds to a different program or service provider if the agency is unable to continue providing the same program or services due to a decrease or loss of federal funds; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(b)(iv): designation of the federal funds and the program or purpose for which the funds will be used as either:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(b)(iv)(A): mandatory under federal or state law;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(b)(iv)(B): high priority; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(b)(iv)(C): low priority.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(c): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(c)(i): "Federal funds" means cash or other money received from the United States government or from other individuals or entities for or on behalf of the United States and deposited with the state treasurer or any agency of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(c)(ii): "Federal funds" includes federal assistance and federal assistance programs, however described.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(d): "Federal funds reauthorization" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(d)(i): the formal submission from an agency to the federal government applying for or seeking reauthorization of federal funds which the state is currently receiving;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(d)(ii): the formal submission from an agency to the federal government applying for or seeking reauthorization to participate in a federal program in which the state is currently participating that will result in federal funds being transferred to an agency; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(d)(iii): that period after the first year of a previously authorized and awarded grant or funding award, during which federal funds are disbursed or are scheduled to be disbursed after the first year because the term of the grant or financial award extends for more than one year.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(e): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(e)(i): "Federal funds request summary" means a document detailing:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(e)(i)(A): the amount of money that is being requested or is available to be received by the state from the federal government for each federal funds reauthorization or new federal funds request;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(e)(i)(B): those federal funds reauthorizations and new federal funds requests that are included as part of the agency's proposed budget for the fiscal year, and the amount of those requests;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(e)(i)(C): the amount of new state money, if any, that will be required to receive the federal funds or participate in the federal program;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(e)(i)(D): the number of additional permanent full-time employees, additional permanent part-time employees, or combination of additional permanent full-time employees and additional permanent part-time employees, if any, that the state estimates are needed in order to receive the federal funds or participate in the federal program;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(e)(i)(E): any requirements that the state must meet as a condition for receiving the federal funds or participating in the federal program; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(e)(i)(F): for each federal funds reauthorization for qualifying federal funds and each new federal funds request for qualifying federal funds, a contingency disclosure and plan, and a state jurisdiction evaluation.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(e)(ii): "Federal funds request summary" includes, if available:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(e)(ii)(A): the letter awarding an agency a grant of federal funds or other official documentation awarding an agency a grant of federal funds; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(e)(ii)(B): a document detailing federal maintenance of effort requirements.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(f): "Federal maintenance of effort requirements" means any matching, level of effort, or earmarking requirements, as defined in Office of Management and Budget requirements, that are imposed on an agency as a condition of receiving federal funds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(g): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(g)(i): "Intergovernmental transfer program" means an existing reimbursement program or category that is authorized by the Medicaid state plan or waiver authority for intergovernmental transfers.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(g)(ii): "Intergovernmental transfer program" does not include the addition of a provider to an existing intergovernmental transfer program.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(h): "Local education agency" or "LEA" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(h)(i): a school district;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(h)(ii): a charter school; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(h)(iii): the Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(i): "New federal funds" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(i)(i): federal assistance or other federal funds that are available from the federal government that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(i)(i)(A): the state is not currently receiving; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(i)(i)(B): exceed the federal funds amount most recently approved by the Legislature by more than 25% for a federal grant or program in which the state is currently participating;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(i)(ii): a federal assistance program or other federal program in which the state is not currently participating; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(i)(iii): a one-time TANF request.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(j): "New federal funds request" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(j)(i): the formal submission from an agency to the federal government:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(j)(i)(A): applying for or otherwise seeking to obtain new federal funds; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(j)(i)(B): applying for or seeking to participate in a new federal program that will result in federal funds being transferred to an agency; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(j)(ii): a one-time TANF request.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(k): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(k)(i): "New state money" means money, whether specifically appropriated by the Legislature or not, that the federal government requires Utah to expend as a condition for receiving the federal funds or participating in the federal program.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(k)(ii): "New state money" includes money expended to meet federal maintenance of effort requirements.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(l): "One-time TANF request" means a proposed expenditure by the Department of Workforce Services from its reserves of federal Temporary Assistance for Needy Families funds:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(l)(i): for a project or program that will last for a fixed amount of time and is not an ongoing project or program of the Department of Workforce Services; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(l)(ii): that is greater than $1,000,000 over the amount most recently approved by the Legislature.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(m): "Qualifying federal funds" means federal funds that are:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(m)(i): greater than 10% of the receiving entity's annual budget; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(m)(ii): greater than $2,000,000.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(n): "State" means the state of Utah and all of its agencies, and any administrative subunits of those agencies.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(o): "State jurisdiction evaluation" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(o)(i): a disclosure of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(o)(i)(A): whether accepting the federal funds or participating in the federal program will require the use of state funds or increase the administrative costs of the state or agency;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(o)(i)(B): the extent to which accepting the federal funds or participating in the federal program will impair or impact the exclusive police power jurisdiction of the state to protect or provide for the health, safety, welfare, and morals of the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(o)(i)(C): the extent to which accepting the federal funds or participating in the federal program will impair or impact the jurisdiction of the state over federal areas within the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(1)(o)(ii): to the extent that accepting the federal funds or participating in the federal program will impair or impact the state's jurisdiction as described in Subsection (1)(o)(i)(B) or (C), an identification of the constitutional authority supporting federal assertion of jurisdiction or authority for the funding, program, or an associated regulation or restriction.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-102(2): When this chapter describes an employee as a "permanent full-time employee" or a "permanent part-time employee," it is not intended to, and may not be construed to, affect the employee's status as an at-will employee.


Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-103 Scope and applicability of chapter.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-103(1): Except as otherwise provided by a statute superseding provisions of this chapter by explicit reference to this chapter, the provisions of this chapter apply to each agency and govern each federal funds request.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-103(2): 53-2a-204 The governor need not seek legislative review or approval of federal funds received by the state if:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-103(2)(a): the governor has declared a state of emergency; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-103(2)(b): 53-2a-204 the federal funds are received to assist victims of the state of emergency under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-201 Legislative appropriation subcommittees to review certain federal funds reauthorizations -- Executive appropriations review -- Legislative approval.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-201(1): 63J-1-201 The Governor's Office of Planning and Budget shall annually prepare and submit a federal funds request summary for each agency to the Legislative Fiscal Analyst at the same time the governor submits the confidential draft budget under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-201(2): JR3-2-402
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-201(2)(a): JR3-2-402 The Legislative Fiscal Analyst, as directed by the Executive Appropriations Committee, may include federal funds in the base budget appropriations act or acts, when those acts are prepared as provided in
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-201(2)(b): The Legislative Fiscal Analyst shall submit a federal funds request summary for each agency to the legislative appropriations subcommittee responsible for that agency's budget for review during each annual general session.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-201(3): Each legislative appropriations subcommittee shall review the federal funds request summary and may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-201(3)(a): recommend that the agency accept the federal funds or participate in the federal program for the fiscal year under consideration; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-201(3)(b): recommend that the agency not accept the federal funds or not participate in the federal program for the fiscal year under consideration.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-201(4): The Legislative Executive Appropriations Committee shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-201(4)(a): review each subcommittee's recommendation;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-201(4)(b): determine whether or not the agency should be authorized to accept the federal funds or participate in the federal program; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-201(4)(c): direct the Legislative Fiscal Analyst to include or exclude those federal funds and federal programs in an annual appropriations act for approval by the Legislature.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-201(5): Legislative approval of an appropriations act containing federal funds constitutes legislative approval of the federal grants or awards associated with the federal funds for the purposes of compliance with the requirements of this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-202 Governor to approve certain new federal funds requests.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-202(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-202(1)(a): Before obligating the state to accept or receive new federal funds or to participate in a new federal program, and no later than three months after submitting a new federal funds request, and, where possible, before formally submitting the new federal funds request, an executive branch agency shall submit a federal funds request summary to the governor or the governor's designee for approval or rejection when:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-202(1)(a)(i): the state will receive total payments of $1,000,000 or less per year if the new federal funds request is approved;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-202(1)(a)(ii): receipt of the new federal funds will require no additional permanent full-time employees, permanent part-time employees, or combination of additional permanent full-time employees and permanent part-time employees; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-202(1)(a)(iii): no new state money will be required to match the new federal funds or to implement the new federal program for which the grant is issued.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-202(1)(b): The Governor's Office of Planning and Budget shall report each new federal funds request that is approved by the governor or the governor's designee and each new federal funds request granted by the federal government to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-202(1)(b)(i): the Legislature's Executive Appropriations Committee;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-202(1)(b)(ii): the Office of the Legislative Fiscal Analyst; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-202(1)(b)(iii): the Office of Legislative Research and General Counsel.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-202(2): The governor or the governor's designee shall approve or reject each new federal funds request submitted under the authority of this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-202(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-202(3)(a): If the governor or the governor's designee approves the new federal funds request, the executive branch agency may accept the new federal funds or participate in the new federal program.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-202(3)(b): If the governor or the governor's designee rejects the new federal funds request, the executive branch agency may not accept the new federal funds or participate in the new federal program.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-202(4): (4)(a); (4)(b); (4)(c) If an executive branch agency fails to obtain the governor's or the governor's designee's approval under this section, the governor may require the agency to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-202(4)(a): withdraw the new federal funds request;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-202(4)(b): return the federal funds;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-202(4)(c): withdraw from the federal program; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-202(4)(d): (4)(a); (4)(b); (4)(c) any combination of Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-202(5): If a letter or other official documentation awarding an agency a grant of federal funds is not available to be included in a federal funds request summary submitted to the Governor's Office of Planning and Budget under this section, the agency shall submit to the Governor's Office of Planning and Budget the letter or other official documentation awarding the agency a grant of federal funds before expending the federal funds granted.


Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203 Judicial council to approve certain new federal funds requests.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203(1)(a): Before obligating the state to accept or receive new federal funds or to participate in a new federal program, and no later than three months after submitting a new federal funds request, and, where possible, before formally submitting the new federal funds request, a judicial branch agency shall submit a federal funds request summary to the Judicial Council for its approval or rejection when:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203(1)(a)(i): the state will receive total payments of $1,000,000 or less per year if the new federal funds request is approved;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203(1)(a)(ii): receipt of the new federal funds will require no additional permanent full-time employees, additional permanent part-time employees, or combination of additional permanent full-time employees and permanent part-time employees; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203(1)(a)(iii): no new state money will be required to match the new federal funds or to implement the new federal program for which the grant is issued.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203(1)(b): The Judicial Council shall report each new federal funds request that is approved by it and each new federal funds request granted by the federal government to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203(1)(b)(i): the Legislature's Executive Appropriations Committee;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203(1)(b)(ii): the Office of the Legislative Fiscal Analyst; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203(1)(b)(iii): the Office of Legislative Research and General Counsel.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203(2): The Judicial Council shall approve or reject each new federal funds request submitted to it under the authority of this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203(3)(a): If the Judicial Council approves the new federal funds request, the judicial branch agency may accept the new federal funds or participate in the new federal program.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203(3)(b): If the Judicial Council rejects the new federal funds request, the judicial branch agency may not accept the new federal funds or participate in the new federal program.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203(4): (4)(a); (4)(b); (4)(c) If a judicial branch agency fails to obtain the Judicial Council's approval under this section, the Judicial Council may require the agency to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203(4)(a): withdraw the new federal funds request;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203(4)(b): return the federal funds;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203(4)(c): withdraw from the federal program; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203(4)(d): (4)(a); (4)(b); (4)(c) any combination of Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203(5): If a letter or other official documentation awarding a judicial branch agency a grant of federal funds is not available to be included in a federal funds request summary submitted to the Judicial Council under this section, the judicial branch agency shall submit to the Judicial Council the letter or other official documentation awarding the judicial branch agency a grant of federal funds before expending the federal funds granted.


Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203.5 State Board of Education to approve certain new federal funds requests. 
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203.5(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203.5(1)(a): Before obligating the state to accept or receive new federal funds or to participate in a new federal program, and no later than three months after submitting a new federal funds request, and, where possible, before formally submitting the new federal funds request, the State Board of Education shall review a federal funds request summary of the State Board of Education when:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203.5(1)(a)(i): the state will receive total payments of $1,000,000 or less per year if the new federal funds request is approved;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203.5(1)(a)(ii): receipt of the new federal funds will require no additional permanent full-time employees, additional permanent part-time employees, or a combination of additional permanent full-time employees and permanent part-time employees; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203.5(1)(a)(iii): no new state money will be required to match the new federal funds or to implement the new federal program for which the grant is issued.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203.5(1)(b): The State Board of Education shall approve or reject each new federal funds request reviewed under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203.5(2): The State Board of Education shall report each new federal funds request that is approved by the board and each new federal funds request granted to the board by the federal government to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203.5(2)(a): the Legislature's Executive Appropriations Committee;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203.5(2)(b): the Office of the Legislative Fiscal Analyst; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203.5(2)(c): the Office of Legislative Research and General Counsel.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-203.5(3): If a letter or other official documentation awarding the State Board of Education a grant of federal funds is not available to be included in the federal funds request summary submitted under this section, the letter or other official documentation awarding the State Board of Education a grant of federal funds shall be submitted to the State Board of Education before expending the federal funds granted.


Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204 Legislative review and approval of certain federal funds requests.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(1)(a): "High impact federal funds request" means a new federal funds request that will or could:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(1)(a)(i): result in the state receiving total payments of $10,000,000 or more per year from the federal government;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(1)(a)(ii): require the state to add 11 or more permanent full-time employees, 11 or more permanent part-time employees, or combination of permanent full-time and permanent part-time employees equal to 11 or more in order to receive the new federal funds or participate in the new federal program; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(1)(a)(iii): require the state to expend more than $1,000,000 of new state money in a fiscal year in order to receive or administer the new federal funds or participate in the new federal program.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(1)(b): "Medium impact federal funds request" means a new federal funds request that will or could:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(1)(b)(i): result in the state receiving total payments of more than $1,000,000 but less than $10,000,000 per year from the federal government;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(1)(b)(ii): require the state to add more than zero but less than 11 permanent full-time employees, more than zero but less than 11 permanent part-time employees, or a combination of permanent full-time employees and permanent part-time employees equal to more than zero but less than 11 in order to receive or administer the new federal funds or participate in the new federal program; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(1)(b)(iii): require the state to expend $1 to $1,000,000 of new state money in a fiscal year in order to receive or administer the new federal funds or participate in the new federal program.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(2): 63J-5-201
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(2)(a): 63J-5-201
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(2)(a)(i): 63J-5-201 Before obligating the state to accept or receive new federal funds or to participate in a new federal program under a medium impact federal funds request that was not authorized during a legislative session as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(2)(a)(i)(A): submit the federal funds request summary to the governor, the Judicial Council,  or the State Board of Education,  as appropriate, for approval or rejection; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(2)(a)(i)(B): if the governor, the Judicial Council, or the State Board of Education  approves the new federal funds request, submit the federal funds request summary to the Legislative Executive Appropriations Committee for its review and recommendations.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(2)(a)(ii): The procedures required under Subsection (2)(a)(i) shall be performed, if possible, before the date that the medium impact funds request is formally submitted, but not later than three months after the date of formal submission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(2)(b): The Legislative Executive Appropriations Committee shall review the federal funds request summary and may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(2)(b)(i): recommend that the agency accept the new federal funds;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(2)(b)(ii): recommend that the agency not accept the new federal funds; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(2)(b)(iii): recommend to the governor that the governor call a special session of the Legislature to review and approve or reject the acceptance of the new federal funds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(3): 63J-5-201
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(3)(a): 63J-5-201
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(3)(a)(i): 63J-5-201 Before obligating the state to accept or receive new federal funds or to participate in a new federal program under a high impact federal funds request that was not authorized during a legislative session as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(3)(a)(i)(A): submit the federal funds request summary to the governor, the Judicial Council,  or the State Board of Education,  as appropriate, for approval or rejection; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(3)(a)(i)(B): if the governor, the Judicial Council , or the State Board of Education  approves the new federal funds request, submit the federal funds request summary to the Legislature for its approval or rejection in an annual general session or a special session.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(3)(a)(ii): Except as provided in Subsection (3)(a)(iii), the procedures required under Subsection (3)(a)(i) shall be performed, if possible, before the date that the high impact funds request is formally submitted, but not later than three months after the date of formal submission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(3)(a)(iii): For a high impact federal funds request for the Medical Assistance Program, commonly known as Medicaid, or the Children's Health Insurance Program, the procedures required under Subsection (3)(a)(i) shall be performed, if possible, before the date that the high impact funds request is formally submitted, but not later than the end of the earlier of the next annual general session or special session of the Legislature after the date of formal submission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(3)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(3)(b)(i): If the Legislature approves the new federal funds request, the agency may accept the new federal funds or participate in the new federal program.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(3)(b)(ii): If the Legislature fails to approve the new federal funds request, the agency may not accept the new federal funds or participate in the new federal program.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(4): If an agency fails to comply with the procedures of this section or fails to obtain the Legislature's approval:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(4)(a): the governor, the Judicial Council,  or the State Board of Education,  as appropriate, may require the agency to withdraw the new federal funds request or refuse or return the new federal funds;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(4)(b): the Legislature may, if federal law allows, opt out or decline to participate in the new federal program or decline to receive the new federal funds; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(4)(c): the Legislature may reduce the agency's General Fund appropriation in an amount less than, equal to, or greater than the amount of federal funds received by the agency.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-204(5): If a letter or other official documentation awarding an agency a grant of federal funds is not available to be included in the agency's federal funds request summary to the governor, the Judicial Council, or the State Board of Education, as appropriate, under this section, the agency shall submit to the governor, the Judicial Council, or the State Board of Education, as appropriate, the letter or other official documentation awarding the agency a grant of federal funds before expending the federal funds granted.


Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-205 Federal funds awards that exceed approved appropriations.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Each agency that receives federal funds greater than the amount approved through the process provided for in this chapter may, using those excess funds, expend up to 25% in excess of the of the amount approved if:Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-205(1): receipt or use of the excess federal funds will not require the addition of one or more permanent full-time employees or permanent part-time employees;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-205(2): no new state money will be required to match the excess federal funds; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-205(3): receipt or use of the excess federal funds will not require the state to comply with new requirements or conditions in order to receive the federal funds or to participate in the federal program.


Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-206 Intergovernmental transfers for Medicaid.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-206(1): (2); (3); 26B-3-130 Subject to Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-206(2): (1); 26B-3-130(3); 63J-5-204(3); (4); (5) Notwithstanding Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-206(3): 63J-5-201
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-206(3)(a): 63J-5-201 Beginning on July 1, 2017, an intergovernmental transfer program created before July 1, 2017, is subject to the federal funds review process of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-206(3)(b): The addition of a new participant into an existing intergovernmental transfer program, or the addition by the department of a nursing care facility or a non-state government entity to the Nursing Care Facility Non-State Government-Owned Upper Payment Limit program, is not subject to the requirements of this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-301 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-301(1): "Federal receipts" means the federal financial assistance, as defined in 31 U.S.C. Sec. 7501, that is reported as part of a single audit.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-301(2): "Qualifying agency" means an agency that, in a single fiscal year, has federal receipts composing more than 33% of the agency's total budget.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-301(3): "Single audit" means the same as that term is defined in 31 U.S.C. Sec. 7501.


Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-302 Federal funds contingency plan.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-302(1): A qualifying agency shall prepare a federal funds contingency plan that meets the requirements described in Subsection (2).
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-302(2): A federal funds contingency plan shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-302(2)(a): identify short-term and long-term risks to the agency if there is a reduction in the amount or value of federal funds the agency receives;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-302(2)(b): identify short-term and long-term strategies the agency may use to respond to the risks described in Subsection (2)(a); and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-302(2)(c): designate agency personnel who are responsible for implementing the strategies described in Subsection (2)(b).
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-302(3): A qualifying agency shall update the agency's federal funds contingency plan:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-302(3)(a): at least every other year; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-302(3)(b): in any year in which the qualifying agency submits a new federal funds request that exceeds $10,000,000.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-302(4): On or before December 31 of each year that a qualifying agency prepares a federal funds contingency plan or an update to a federal funds contingency plan, the qualifying agency shall provide a copy of the contingency plan or update to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-302(4)(a): the Governor's Office of Planning and Budget;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-302(4)(b): the Executive Appropriations Committee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-5-302(4)(c): the Legislative Fiscal Analyst.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 63J - Chapter 6 - Tax Anticipation Notes Act
************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 63J-6-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Tax Anticipation Notes Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 63J-6-201 Borrowing authorized -- Limitation -- Issuance of notes -- Maximum term.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The state treasurer may borrow money for the state in anticipation of (a) income or revenue from taxes, whether the taxes are specific, ad valorem, excise, sales, income, franchise, or fees for the current fiscal year, or that portion of the taxes not collected or previously anticipated at the time of borrowing, and (b) other non-tax revenues of the state, in a principal sum not greater than 75% of such income or revenue which the director of the Division of Finance certifies to the state treasurer are to be reasonably anticipated to be collected during the current fiscal year.  Each loan shall be evidenced by the issuance and sale of tax and revenue anticipation notes of the state, for fixed periods not to exceed 12 months or the end of the current fiscal year, whichever is sooner.

Utah Code Annotated § 63J-6-202 Issuance -- Financing plan required -- Contents -- Order setting terms of notes -- Recitations in notes -- Report of sales -- Disposition of proceeds.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-6-202(1): 63J-6-201 If the state treasurer considers it to be in the best interests of the state to issue tax and revenue anticipation notes under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-6-202(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-6-202(2)(a): Prior to the issuance and sale of any tax or revenue anticipation note to other than a state fund or account, the state treasurer shall prepare a written plan of financing which shall be filed with the governor.  The plan of financing shall provide for the terms and conditions under which the notes will be issued, sold, and delivered, the taxes or revenues to be anticipated, the maximum amount of notes which may be outstanding at any one time under the plan of financing, the sources of payment of the notes issued pursuant to the plan of financing, and all other details relating to the issuance, sale, and delivery of the notes.  The sources of payment of the notes issued pursuant to the plan of financing may include the proceeds of sale of notes issued to refund outstanding tax or revenue anticipation notes and to pay accrued interest on them.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-6-202(2)(b): The plan of financing shall specify the rates of interest, if any, on the notes or a method, formula, or index pursuant to which the interest rates on the notes may be determined during the time the notes are outstanding.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-6-202(2)(c): The state treasurer may include in the plan of financing the terms and conditions of arrangements entered into by the state treasurer on behalf of the state with financial and other institutions for letters of credit, standby letters of credit, reimbursement agreements, and remarketing, indexing, and tender agent agreements to secure the tax anticipation notes, including payment from any legally available source of fees, charges, or other amounts coming due under the agreements entered into by the treasurer.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-6-202(3): The interest, form, manner of execution, payment, manner of sale, prices at, above, or below face value, and all details of issuance of the notes shall be set forth in an order of the state treasurer.  The order and the details set forth in the order shall conform with any applicable plan of financing and with this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-6-202(4): Each note shall recite that it is a valid obligation of the state and that the faith and credit of the state are pledged for the payment of the principal of and interest on the note from the revenues of the fiscal year in which the note is issued in accordance with its terms and the constitution and laws of Utah.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-6-202(5): Immediately upon the completion of any sale, the state treasurer shall make a verified return of the sale to the state auditor, specifying the amount of notes sold, the persons to whom the notes were sold, and the price, terms, and conditions of the sale.  Immediately upon the sale of any notes, the state treasurer shall credit the proceeds of sale, other than accrued interest, to the General Fund.


Utah Code Annotated § 63J-6-203 Redemption account -- Creation -- Sources -- Use -- Investment -- Income.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-6-203(1): There is created a restricted account within the General Fund known as the "Tax and Revenue Anticipation Note Redemption Account."  When any notes have been issued in anticipation of income or revenue under this chapter, not less than two days before the principal and interest on the notes comes due, income or revenue realized from the tax or nontax sources specified in the approved plan of financing to be anticipated or from any other source of money legally available for such purpose shall be placed in the restricted account so that the amount in the restricted account is sufficient to pay the principal amount of all notes outstanding, together with interest on them.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-6-203(2): The money in the restricted account is appropriated solely for the payment of the principal of and interest on the notes issued under this chapter.  The payment of the principal and interest on the notes issued under this chapter is not limited solely to the income and revenues from the specific tax or nontax sources in anticipation of which the notes were issued.  Accrued interest received upon the sale of the notes shall be deposited by the state treasurer in the restricted account.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-6-203(3): Title 51, Chapter 7, State Money Management Act The state treasurer may invest all money in the restricted account in accordance with


Utah Code Annotated § 63J-6-204 Expenses of notes paid from proceeds.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
All expenses incident to the issuance of tax and revenue anticipation notes under this chapter shall be paid from the proceeds of sale of the notes credited to the General Fund.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 63J - Chapter 7 - Grants from Persons and Corporations
**********************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1): As used in this chapter:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(a)(i): "Agency" means a department, division, committee, commission, council, court, or other administrative subunit of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(a)(ii): "Agency" includes executive branch entities and judicial branch entities.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(a)(iii): "Agency" does not mean higher education institutions or political subdivisions.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(b)(i): "Grant" means cash or other money donated to an agency.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(b)(ii): "Grant" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(b)(ii)(A): a reauthorization of an existing grant; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(b)(ii)(B): a donation, regardless of whether it is subject to a formal grant agreement.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(b)(iii): "Grant" does not mean:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(b)(iii)(A): money appropriated to an agency by the Legislature;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(b)(iii)(B): money received from the United States government;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(b)(iii)(C): money legally required to be paid to the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(b)(iii)(D): money legally required to be repaid by the state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(b)(iii)(E): revenues otherwise designated by law for deposit into another fund or account.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(c): "Grantor" means the individual, group of individuals, foundation, corporation, or public or private organization making the grant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(d): "Grant reauthorization" means the formal submission from an agency to the grantor applying for reauthorization or seeking reauthorization of a grant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(e): "Grant summary" means a document detailing:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(e)(i): the amount of money that is being requested or is available to be received by the agency from a grant;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(e)(ii): the duration of the grant and provisions for its reauthorization or extension, if any;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(e)(iii): the name of the grantor;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(e)(iv): the purpose of the grant, including, in detail, any programs, resources, and positions required to be funded by the grant;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(e)(v): any requirements that the agency must meet as a condition to receive or participate in the grant; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(e)(vi): the amount of state money, if any, that will be required in order to obtain the grant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(f): "New state money" means money, whether specifically appropriated by the Legislature or not, that the grantor requires Utah to expend as a condition for receiving the grant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(1)(g): "State" means the state of Utah and all of its agencies, and any administrative subunits of those agencies.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-101(2): When this chapter describes an employee as a "permanent full-time employee" or a "permanent part-time employee," it is not intended to, and may not be construed to, affect the employee's status as an at-will employee.

Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-201 Governor to approve certain grant requests.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-201(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-201(1)(a): Before obligating the state to accept or receive a grant, an executive branch agency shall submit a grant summary to the governor or the governor's designee for approval or rejection when:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-201(1)(a)(i): the executive branch agency would receive a grant of at least $10,000 but no more than $50,000 if the grant is approved;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-201(1)(a)(ii): receipt of the grant will require no additional permanent full-time employees, permanent part-time employees, or combination of additional permanent full-time employees and permanent part-time employees; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-201(1)(a)(iii): no new state money will be required to match the grant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-201(1)(b): The Governor's Office of Planning and Budget shall report each grant authorized under this section to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-201(1)(b)(i): the Legislature's Executive Appropriations Committee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-201(1)(b)(ii): the Office of the Legislative Fiscal Analyst.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-201(2): The governor or the governor's designee shall approve or reject each grant submitted under the authority of this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-201(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-201(3)(a): If the governor or the governor's designee approves the grant, the executive branch agency may accept the grant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-201(3)(b): If the governor or the governor's designee rejects the grant, the executive branch agency may not accept the grant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-201(4): If an executive branch agency fails to obtain the governor's or the governor's designee's approval under this section, the governor may require the agency to return the grant.


Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-202 Judicial council to approve certain grant requests.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-202(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-202(1)(a): Before obligating the state to accept or receive a grant, a judicial branch agency shall submit a grant summary to the Judicial Council for its approval or rejection when:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-202(1)(a)(i): the state would receive a grant of at least $10,000 but no more than $50,000 if the grant is approved;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-202(1)(a)(ii): receipt of the grant will require no additional permanent full-time employees, additional permanent part-time employees, or combination of additional permanent full-time employees and permanent part-time employees; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-202(1)(a)(iii): no new state money will be required to match the grant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-202(1)(b): The Judicial Council shall report each grant authorized under this section to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-202(1)(b)(i): the Legislature's Executive Appropriations Committee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-202(1)(b)(ii): the Office of the Legislative Fiscal Analyst.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-202(2): The Judicial Council shall approve or reject each grant submitted under the authority of this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-202(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-202(3)(a): If the Judicial Council approves the grant, the judicial branch agency may accept the grant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-202(3)(b): If the Judicial Council rejects the grant, the judicial branch agency may not accept the grant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-202(4): If a judicial branch agency fails to obtain the Judicial Council's approval under this section, the Judicial Council may require the agency to return the grant.


Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203 Legislative review and approval of certain grant requests.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(1)(a): "High impact grant" means a grant that will or could:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(1)(a)(i): result in the state receiving total payments of $1,000,000 or more per year from the grantor;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(1)(a)(ii): require the state to add 11 or more permanent full-time employees, 11 or more permanent part-time employees, or combination of permanent full-time employees and permanent part-time employees equal to 11 or more in order to receive the grant; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(1)(a)(iii): require the state to expend more than $1,000,000 of new state money in a fiscal year in order to receive or administer the grant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(1)(b): "Medium impact grant" means a grant that will or could:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(1)(b)(i): result in the state receiving total payments of more than $50,000 but less than $1,000,000 per year from the grantor;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(1)(b)(ii): require the state to add more than zero but less than 11 permanent full-time employees, more than zero but less than 11 permanent part-time employees, or a combination of permanent full-time employees and permanent part-time employees equal to more than zero but less than 11 in order to receive or administer the grant; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(1)(b)(iii): require the state to expend $1 to $1,000,000 of new state money in a fiscal year in order to receive or administer the grant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(2)(a): Before obligating the state to accept or receive a medium impact grant, and, where possible, before formally submitting a request for a medium impact grant to the grantor, an agency shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(2)(a)(i): submit the grant summary to the governor or the Judicial Council, as appropriate, for approval or rejection; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(2)(a)(ii): if the governor or Judicial Council approves the grant, submit the grant summary to the Legislative Executive Appropriations Committee for its review and recommendations.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(2)(b): The Legislative Executive Appropriations Committee shall review the grant summary and may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(2)(b)(i): recommend that the agency accept the grant;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(2)(b)(ii): recommend that the agency not accept the grant; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(2)(b)(iii): recommend to the governor that the governor call a special session of the Legislature to review and approve or reject the acceptance of the grant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(3): (3)
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(3)(a): Before obligating the state to accept or receive a high impact grant, and, where possible, before formally submitting a request for a high impact grant to the grantor, an agency shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(3)(a)(i): submit the grant summary to the governor or Judicial Council, as appropriate, for approval or rejection; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(3)(a)(ii): if the governor or Judicial Council approves the grant, submit the grant summary to the Legislature for its approval or rejection in an annual general session or a special session.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(3)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(3)(b)(i): If the Legislature approves the grant, the agency may accept the grant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(3)(b)(ii): If the Legislature fails to approve the grant, the agency may not accept the grant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(3)(c): (3) If an agency fails to obtain the Legislature's approval under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(3)(c)(i): the governor or Judicial Council, as appropriate, may require the agency to return the grant;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(3)(c)(ii): the Legislature may direct the agency to return the grant to the grantor; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-7-203(3)(c)(iii): the Legislature may reduce the agency's appropriation in an amount less than, equal to, or greater than the amount of the grant received by the agency.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 63J - Chapter 8 - State of Utah Resource Management Plan for Federal Lands
******************************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 63J-8-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as "State of Utah Resource Management Plan for Federal Lands."

Utah Code Annotated § 63J-8-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 63J-8-102(1): "ACEC" means an area of critical environmental concern as defined in 43 U.S.C. Sec. 1702.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-8-102(2): "AUM" means animal unit months, a unit of grazing forage.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-8-102(3): "BLM" means the United States Bureau of Land Management.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-8-102(4): "BLM recommended wilderness" means a wilderness study area recommended for wilderness designation in the final report of the president of the United States to the United States Congress in 1993.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-8-102(5): "Federal land use designation" means one or a combination of the following congressional or federal actions included in proposed congressional land use legislation:
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-8-102(5)(a): designation of wilderness within the National Wilderness Preservation System;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-8-102(5)(b): designation of a national conservation area;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-8-102(5)(c): designation of a watercourse within the National Wild and Scenic River System;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-8-102(5)(d): designation of an ACEC;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-8-102(5)(e): designation of a national monument in accordance with the Antiquities Act or by Congress;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-8-102(5)(f): designation of a national park within the National Park System;
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-8-102(5)(g): designation of a national recreational area; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-8-102(5)(h): any other designation, classification, categorization, reservation, withdrawal, or similar action that has the purpose or effect of eliminating, restricting, or reducing energy and mineral development, motorized travel, grazing, active vegetation management, or any other traditional multiple use on public land.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-8-102(6): "FLPMA" means the Federal Land Policy and Management Act of 1976, 43 U.S.C. Sec. 1701 et seq.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-8-102(7): "Forest Service" means the United States Forest Service within the United States Department of Agriculture.
Utah Code Annotated § 63J-8-102(8): (8)(a); (b) "Green River Energy Zone" means the lands described as follows in Subsections
